Mason\nHansen\n\nNUCLEAR\n\nINSTITUTE\n\nCambridge,\n\nAugust,\n\nENGINEERING\nOF\n\nTECHNOLOGY\n\nMassachusetts\n\n1964\n\nWork\nSponsored\nin Part\nby\nM. I. T. Center\nfor Space\nResearch\nunder\nNASA Grant\nNsG-496\n\n2\n\nREACTIVITY CHANGES DURING STARTUP\nIN LARGE NUCLEAR ROCKETS\nby\nWinston W. Little,\n\nJr.\n\nSubmitted to the Department of Nuclear Engineering on July 29, 1964 in\npartial fulfillment\nof the requirements for the degree of Doctor of Science\nin Nuclear Engineering.\n\nThe objective of this thesis was to investigate some of the nucleonic\nproblems associated with starting large, solid core nuclear rockets fueled\nwith uranium-235.\nPrimary emphasis was placed on obtaining the reactivity variations during startup induced by changes in hydrogen density and\ncore temperature.\nA detailed nucleonic analysis of a nuclear rocket during startup\nwould be extremely complex and time consuming. In order to make the\nproblem tractable, the following procedure was adopted. First, the\nmaterial properties, such as core temperature, hydrogen density, etc.,\nwere computed as a function of time during startup for a specified power\nand flow rate buildup.\nUsing these time dependent properties, the reactivity variations during startup were calculated using a diffusion theory\nmodel with 55 energy groups. The spatial dimensions were approximated\nby assuming V2_(E) = -B2_(E).\nSuch an assumption\nshould\nbe permissible\nin light\nof the fact\nthat changes\nin core\ntemperature\nand hydrogen\ndensity\nhave\nlittle\neffect\non the spatial\ndistribution,\nbut have\na significant\neffect\non\nthe energy\ndistribution.\nIt was\nfound\nthat\nlarge\nthermal\nnuclear\nrocket\nreactors\n{C/U\n= 2500}\nare\nmuch\nmore\nsensitive\nto changes\nin hydrogen\ndensity\nand core\ntemperature\nthan\nsmall\nnuclear\nrockets\n(C/U\n= 250}.\nThe large\nreactivity\ncoefficients\npresent\nin thermal\nreactors\ncause\nboth large\n(N-$13.)\nand rapid\n(~-$1\n./sec)\nreactivity\nvariations\nduring\nthe quick\nstartups\ncontemplated\nfor nuclear\nrockets.\nThis\nproblem\ncan be ameliorated\nto some\ndegree\nby\nadding\na nuclear\npoison\nto the core.\nHowever,\nany poison\nhas the adverse\nside\neffect\nof decreasing\nthe worth\nof an external\ncontrol\nrod system\nby\ndecreasing\nthe leakage.\nAn estimation\nof the worth\nof an external\ncontrol\nrod\nsystem\nwas\nobtained\nusing\na one-dimensional\nnucleonics\nmodel\nwith three\nenergy\ngroups.\nIt was found\nthat thermal\nreactors\nwould\nrequire\nvery\nthick\nand\nheavy\nreflectors\nin order\nto control\nthe reactivity\nvariation\nduring\nstartup.\nThesis\n\nSupervisors:\nProfessor\nProfessor\n\nEdward\nKent\nF.\n\nA. Mason,\nProfessor\nHansen,\nAssistant\n\nof Nuclear\nEngineering\nProfessor\nof Nuclear\nEngineering\n\nI\n1\n\nACKNOWLEDGMENTS\n\nThe\n\nauthor\n\nProfessors\nvaluable\n\nwishes\n\nEdward\ntime.\n\ncriticisms\n\nA.\n\nBoth\n\nwhich\nThe\n\ngave\n\nauthor\n\nis\n\nfor\n\nthe\n\nalso\n\nperformed\n\nat\n\nalso\n\nin the\nThe\n\nResearch\n\nform\nwork\nunder\n\nThe\n\nwork\n\nKent\n\nHansen\n\nfor\n\nto the\n\nto\n\nthe\n\nand\n\nuse\n\nof their\n\nconstructive\n\nauthor.\n\nto Dr.\n\nRichard\n\nK. Fluid flow and rocket technology is often expressed in English units, whereas the metric system\nis universally employed in reactor physics. For convenience, the metric\nsystem, including both the MKS and CGS units, is used throughout this\nthesis.\nA table is given in Appendix F for conversion to the more\ncommon English
